envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\\\";\\n8: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n9: import \\\"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\\\";\\n10: \\n11: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n12: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n13: \\n14: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n15: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n16: \\n17: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n18: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExtProcProto\\\";\\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n20: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n22: \\n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\\n153: \\n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\\n156:   // for \\\"host\\\", \\\":authority\\\", \\\":scheme\\\", \\\":method\\\", and headers that start\\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\\n159:   // (which is usually \\\"x-envoy\\\").\\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \\\"host\\\" or \\\":authority\\\" may not in itself\\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n22: \\n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n91: // server\\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n95: //\\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n98: // name.\\n99: //\\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\\n102:   reserved 4;\\n103: \\n104:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n105: \\n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n107:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n109: \\n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n22: \n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n24: // External Processing Filter\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n26: \n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n28: \n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n31: //\n32: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n33: \n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n36: //\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n41: //\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n44: // and how it should be processed.\n45: //\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n47: //\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n53: //\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\n57: //\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n63: //   to SEND.\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n118: \n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n122: \n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n129: \n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n136: \n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n147:     gte {}\n148:   }];\n149: \n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n151:   // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n152:   string stat_prefix = 8;\n153: \n154:   // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n155:   // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n156:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n157:   // with the header prefix set via\n158:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n159:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n160:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n161:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n162:   // route to be recomputed, set the\n163:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n164:   // field to true in the same response.\n165:   config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n166: \n167:   // Specify the upper bound of\n168:   // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n169:   // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n170:   google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n171:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n172:     gte {}\n173:   }];\n174: \n175:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n176:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n177:   // field is set in an external processor response.\n178:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n179: \n180:   // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n181:   // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n182:   HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n183: \n184:   // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n185:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n186:   // ext_proc filter name.\n187:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n188: \n189:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n190:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n191:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n192:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n193:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n194:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n195: \n196:   // If set to true, ignore the\n197:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n198:   // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n199:   // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n202: \n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n205: \n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n208:   // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n209:   //\n210:   // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n211:   // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n212:   //\n213:   // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n214:   // This also means that\n215:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n216:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n217:   //\n218:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n219:   //\n220:   // .. warning::\n221:   //\n222:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n223:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n224:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n225:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n226:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n227:   //\n228:   bool observability_mode = 17;\n229: }\n230: \n231: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n232: // dynamic metadata. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n253:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n255: }\n256: \n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n259: //\n260: // This works as below:\n261: //\n262: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n263: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n264: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n265: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n266: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n267: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n268: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n269: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n270:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n271:   // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n272:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n273: \n274:   // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n275:   // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n276:   type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n277: }\n278: \n279: // Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n280: // virtual host or cluster.\n281: message ExtProcPerRoute {\n282:   oneof override {\n283:     option (validate.required) = true;\n284: \n285:     // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n286:     // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n287:     bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n288: \n289:     // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n290:     // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n291:     // flag set in a less-specific one.\n292:     ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n293:   }\n294: }\n295: \n296: // Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n297: // [#next-free-field: 8]\n298: message ExtProcOverrides {\n299:   // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n300:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n301: \n302:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n303:   // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n304:   bool async_mode = 2;\n305: \n306:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n307:   // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n308:   // ``request_attributes`` field.\n309:   repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n310: \n311:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n312:   // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n313:   // ``response_attributes`` field.\n314:   repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n315: \n316:   // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n317:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n318: \n319:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n320:   // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n321:   // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n322:   // config used. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n300: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n301: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n302: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n303: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n304: //   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n305: //      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n306: message HeaderForwardingRules {\n307:   // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n308:   // processing server. state, Buffer::Instance& data, bool end_stream) {\\n388:   if (end_stream) {\\n389:     state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\\n390:   }\\n391:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\\n392:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\\\");\\n393:     data.drain(data.length());\\n394:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n395:   }\\n396:   if    // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\\n407:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\\n408:     // buffer limit.\\n409:     state.setPaused(true);\\n410:     state.requestWatermark();\\n411:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\\n412:   }\\n413: \\n414:   FilterDataStatus mode works as follows:\\n445:     //\\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \\\"moves\\\" the data into a new buffer, which it\\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n449:     // out of memory.\\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n452:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n454:     // injected.)\\n455:     //\\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n466:       // Fall through\\n467:       break;\\n468:     }\\n469: \\n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n474: \\n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n476:     if (end_stream) {\\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n480:     } else {\\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n482:     }\\n483:     break;\\n484:   }\\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n487:     //\\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. progress for partial mode\\\");\\n512:       state.setPaused(true);\\n513:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n514:     } else {\\n515:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n516:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\\n517:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\\n518:         // to the processor.\\n519:         bool terminate;\\n520:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\\n521:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\\n522:         if (terminate) ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n530:   default:\\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n532:     break;\\n533:   }\\n534: \\n535:   return result;\\n536: }\\n537: \\n538: std::pair<bool, state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n390:   }\n391:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\n392:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\");\n393:     data.drain(data.length());\n394:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n395:   }\n396:   if (processing_complete_) {\n397:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Continuing (processing complete)\");\n398:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n399:   }\n400: \n401:   if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\n402:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\");\n403:     // We don't know what to do with the body until the response comes back.\n404:     // We must buffer it in case we need it when that happens.\n405:     // Raise a watermark to prevent a buffer overflow until the response comes back.\n406:     // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\n407:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\n408:     // buffer limit.\n409:     state.setPaused(true);\n410:     state.requestWatermark();\n411:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n412:   }\n413: \n414:   FilterDataStatus result;\n415:   switch (state.bodyMode()) {\n416:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED:\n417:     if (end_stream) {\n418:       switch (openStream()) {\n419:       case StreamOpenState::Error:\n420:         return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n421:       case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n422: to send the buffer\n429:       ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending request body message\");\n430:       state.addBufferedData(data);\n431:       auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), end_stream);\n432:       sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n433:       // Since we just just moved the data into the buffer, return NoBuffer\n434:       // so that we do not buffer this chunk twice.\n435:       state.setPaused(true);\n436:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n437:       break;\n438:     }\n439:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onData: Buffering\");\n440:     state.setPaused(true);\n441:     result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndBuffer;\n442:     break;\n443:   case ProcessingMode::STREAMED: {\n444:     // STREAMED body mode works as follows:\n445:     //\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \"moves\" the data into a new buffer, which it\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\n449:     // out of memory.\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\n452:     // into the filter chain using \"inject**codedData\". (The processor may respond indicating that\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\n454:     // injected.)\n455:     //\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n466:       // Fall through\n467:       break;\n468:     }\n469: \n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\n474: \n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\n476:     if (end_stream) {\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n480:     } else {\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n482:     }\n483:     break;\n484:   }\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\n487:     //\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\n490:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\n491:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\n492:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\n493:     // buffered mode.\n494:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\n495:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\n496:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\n497:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\n498:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\n499:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\n500:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\n501:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Partial buffer limit reached\");\n502:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\n503:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\n504:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\n505:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n506:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\n507:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\n508:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\n509:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\n510:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n511:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Call in progress for partial mode\");\n512:       state.setPaused(true);\n513:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n514:     } else {\n515:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n516:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\n517:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\n518:         // to the processor.\n519:         bool terminate;\n520:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\n521:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\n522:         if (terminate) {\n523:           return chunk_result;\n524:         }\n525:       }\n526:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n527:     }\n528:     break;\n529:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\n530:   default:\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n532:     break;\n533:   }\n534: \n535:   return result;\n536: }\n537: \n538: std::pair<bool, Http::FilterDataStatus> It\\n537:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n538:     // out of memory.\\n539:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n540:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n541:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n542:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n543:     // injected.)\\n544:     //\\n545:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n546:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. sendDataInObservabilityMode(data, state, end_stream);\n475:   }\n476: \n477:   if (end_stream) {\n478:     state.setCompleteBodyAvailable(true);\n479:   }\n480:   if (state.bodyReplaced()) {\n481:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Clearing body chunk because CONTINUE_AND_REPLACE was returned\");\n482:     data.drain(data.length());\n483:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n484:   }\n485:   if (processing_complete_) {\n486:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Continuing (processing complete)\");\n487:     return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n488:   }\n489: \n490:   if (state.callbackState() == ProcessorState::CallbackState::HeadersCallback) {\n491:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Header processing still in progress -- holding body data\");\n492:     // We don't know what to do with the body until the response comes back.\n493:     // We must buffer it in case we need it when that happens.\n494:     // Raise a watermark to prevent a buffer overflow until the response comes back.\n495:     // When end_stream is true, we need to StopIterationAndWatermark as well to stop the\n496:     // ActiveStream from returning error when the last chunk added to stream buffer exceeds the\n497:     // buffer limit.\n498:     state.setPaused(true);\n499:     state.requestWatermark();\n500:     return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndWatermark;\n501:   }\n502: \n503:   FilterDataStatus result;\n504:   switch (state.bodyMode()) {\n505:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED:\n506:     if (end_stream) {\n507:       switch (openStream()) {\n508:       case StreamOpenState::Error:\n509:         return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n510:       case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n511:         return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n512:       case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n513:         // Fall through\n514:         break;\n515:       }\n516: \n517:       // The body has been buffered and we need to send the buffer\n518:       ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Sending request body message\");\n519:       state.addBufferedData(data);\n520:       auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, *state.bufferedData(), end_stream);\n521:       sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedBodyCallback, req);\n522:       // Since we just just moved the data into the buffer, return NoBuffer\n523:       // so that we do not buffer this chunk twice.\n524:       state.setPaused(true);\n525:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n526:       break;\n527:     }\n528:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"onData: Buffering\");\n529:     state.setPaused(true);\n530:     result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationAndBuffer;\n531:     break;\n532:   case ProcessingMode::STREAMED: {\n533:     // STREAMED body mode works as follows:\n534:     //\n535:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \"moves\" the data into a new buffer, which it\n536:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\n537:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\n538:     // out of memory.\n539:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\n540:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\n541:     // into the filter chain using \"inject**codedData\". (The processor may respond indicating that\n542:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\n543:     // injected.)\n544:     //\n545:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\n546:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\n547:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\n548:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\n549:     switch (openStream()) {\n550:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\n551:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n552:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\n553:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n554:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\n555:       // Fall through\n556:       break;\n557:     }\n558: \n559:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\n560:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\n561:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n562:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\n563: \n564:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\n565:     if (end_stream) {\n566:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\n567:       state.setPaused(true);\n568:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n569:     } else {\n570:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n571:     }\n572:     break;\n573:   }\n574:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\n575:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\n576:     //\n577:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\n578:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\n579:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\n580:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\n581:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\n582:     // buffered mode.\n583:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\n584:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\n585:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\n586:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\n587:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\n588:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\n589:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\n590:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Partial buffer limit reached\");\n591:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\n592:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\n593:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\n594:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\n595:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\n596:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\n597:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\n598:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\n599:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\n600:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Call in progress for partial mode\");\n601:       state.setPaused(true);\n602:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\n603:     } else {\n604:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, Filter::onReceiveMessage(std::unique_ptr<ProcessingResponse>&& r) {\n1042: \n1043:   if (config_->observabilityMode()) {\n1044:     ENVOY_LOG(trace, \"Ignoring received message when observability mode mode works as follows:\\n445:     //\\n446:     // 1) As data callbacks come in to the filter, it \\\"moves\\\" the data into a new buffer, which it\\n447:     // dispatches via gRPC message to the external processor, and then keeps in a queue. It\\n448:     // may request a watermark if the queue is higher than the buffer limit to prevent running\\n449:     // out of memory.\\n450:     // 2) As a result, filters farther down the chain see empty buffers in some data callbacks.\\n451:     // 3) When a response comes back from the external processor, it injects the processor's result\\n452:     // into the filter chain using \\\"inject**codedData\\\". (The processor may respond indicating that\\n453:     // there is no change, which means that the original buffer stored in the queue is what gets\\n454:     // injected.)\\n455:     //\\n456:     // This way, we pipeline data from the proxy to the external processor, and give the processor\\n457:     // the ability to modify each chunk, in order. Doing this any other way would have required\\n458:     // substantial changes to the filter manager. See\\n459:     // https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/16760 for a discussion.\\n460:     switch (openStream()) {\\n461:     case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n462:       return FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n463:     case StreamOpenState::IgnoreError:\\n464:       return FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n465:     case StreamOpenState::Ok:\\n466:       // Fall through\\n467:       break;\\n468:     }\\n469: \\n470:     // Need to first enqueue the data into the chunk queue before sending.\\n471:     auto req = setupBodyChunk(state, data, end_stream);\\n472:     state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n473:     sendBodyChunk(state, ProcessorState::CallbackState::StreamedBodyCallback, req);\\n474: \\n475:     // At this point we will continue, but with no data, because that will come later\\n476:     if (end_stream) {\\n477:       // But we need to stop iteration for the last chunk because it's our last chance to do stuff\\n478:       state.setPaused(true);\\n479:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n480:     } else {\\n481:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n482:     }\\n483:     break;\\n484:   }\\n485:   case ProcessingMode::BUFFERED_PARTIAL:\\n486:     // BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode works as follows:\\n487:     //\\n488:     // 1) As data chunks arrive, we move the data into a new buffer, which we store\\n489:     // in the buffer queue, and continue the filter stream with an empty buffer. This\\n490:     // is the same thing that we do in STREAMING mode.\\n491:     // 2) If end of stream is reached before the queue reaches the buffer limit, we\\n492:     // send the buffered data to the server and essentially behave as if we are in\\n493:     // buffered mode.\\n494:     // 3) If instead the buffer limit is reached before end of stream, then we also\\n495:     // send the buffered data to the server, and raise the watermark to prevent Envoy\\n496:     // from running out of memory while we wait.\\n497:     // 4) It is possible that Envoy will keep sending us data even in that case, so\\n498:     // we must continue to queue data and prepare to re-inject it later.\\n499:     if (state.partialBodyProcessed()) {\\n500:       // We already sent and received the buffer, so everything else just falls through.\\n501:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Partial buffer limit reached\\\");\\n502:       // Make sure that we do not accidentally try to modify the headers before\\n503:       // we continue, which will result in them possibly being sent.\\n504:       state.setHeaders(nullptr);\\n505:       result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n506:     } else if (state.callbackState() ==\\n507:                ProcessorState::CallbackState::BufferedPartialBodyCallback) {\\n508:       // More data came in while we were waiting for a callback result. We need\\n509:       // to queue it and deliver it later in case the callback changes the data.\\n510:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n511:       ENVOY_LOG(trace, \\\"Call in progress for partial mode\\\");\\n512:       state.setPaused(true);\\n513:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n514:     } else {\\n515:       state.enqueueStreamingChunk(data, end_stream);\\n516:       if (end_stream || state.queueOverHighLimit()) {\\n517:         // At either end of stream or when the buffer is full, it's time to send what we have\\n518:         // to the processor.\\n519:         bool terminate;\\n520:         FilterDataStatus chunk_result;\\n521:         std::tie(terminate, chunk_result) = sendStreamChunk(state);\\n522:         if (terminate) {\\n523:           return chunk_result;\\n524:         }\\n525:       }\\n526:       result = FilterDataStatus::StopIterationNoBuffer;\\n527:     }\\n528:     break;\\n529:   case ProcessingMode::NONE:\\n530:   default:\\n531:     result = FilterDataStatus::Continue;\\n532:     break;\\n533:   }\\n534: \\n535:   return result;\\n536: }\\n537: \\n538: std::pair<bool, Http::FilterDataStatus> Filter::sendStreamChunk(ProcessorState& state) {\\n539:   switch (openStream()) {\\n540:   case StreamOpenState::Error:\\n541:     return {true, The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\\n2: \\n3: External Processing\\n4: ===================\\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\\n7: \\n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \\\"external processor,\\\"\\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37:
